<div id="review_1103047796" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103047796" />
    <a title="Nathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5238423-nathan"><img alt="Nathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352775557p2/5238423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1103047796?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/5238423-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=author-female">author-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=rated-5-star">rated-5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5238423-nathan?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103047796" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6618774658522556246"> <a href='http://www.fantasyreviewbarn.com/2014/11/14/fantasy-review-dreamers-pool-by-juliet-marillier/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Review Barn</a><br/><br/>Once upon a time Juliet Marillier wrote a fairy tale and it was wonderful. She didn’t revamp an old classic with a new twist. She didn’t write something like a fairy tale that twists all the tropes around. She didn’t even write a fantasy book with a fairy tale feel to it. She wrote an honest to goodness fairy tale; slightly dark, slightly magical, and completely wonderful.<br/><br/>It starts with a bargain. Blackthorn, who had another name in another time under different circumstances,</span>
  <span id="freeText6618774658522556246" style="display:none"> <a href="http://www.fantasyreviewbarn.com/2014/11/14/fantasy-review-dreamers-pool-by-juliet-marillier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Review Barn</a><br /><br />Once upon a time Juliet Marillier wrote a fairy tale and it was wonderful. She didn’t revamp an old classic with a new twist. She didn’t write something like a fairy tale that twists all the tropes around. She didn’t even write a fantasy book with a fairy tale feel to it. She wrote an honest to goodness fairy tale; slightly dark, slightly magical, and completely wonderful.<br /><br />It starts with a bargain. Blackthorn, who had another name in another time under different circumstances, strikes a deal with a fae; seven years of services for escape from certain death. But the service is not to the fae himself but rather to the service to a community Followed by a man called Grim, or more often Bonehead in the jail they shared, she is to take on her old role of healer and wise women in a new location far from any home she has ever known.<br /><br />Or maybe it starts with a tragedy. A prince eagerly awaiting his unseen soul mate first sees her in the worst of situations; right after the drowning death of one of her handmaidens in a mysterious pond on the princes’ lands. Where ever it starts these three very different people are now tied together in this fairy game – Grim, Blackthorn and the Prince Oran.<br /><br />Let’s talk Blackthorn first as it is her story. A redemption tale? Perhaps, we first meet her in jail awaiting her time. A revenge story? Certainly not, as much as she wishes otherwise. The very nature of her bargain keeps her from the vengeance she desires for unknown past crimes. Worse, it forces her to help any who seek it despite her lack of desire to do much for anyone. But she is good at what she does, earns respect quickly and becomes an valuable member of her new community. She is that rare middle aged women who never seems to show in fantasy; the young see her as a crone already but she knows she has a ways to go before she hits that label.<br /><br />Now Grim. Silent giant, thought to be touched in the head. A violent past implied. Destined to be either a gentle giant or a thug…in another story. But here is just a very human character. He has anger issues but controls them, makes friends in some places and not others, follows Blackthorn like a guard dog but doesn’t hover or attempt to control.<br /><br />Finally Oran. Idealist. Dreamer. But more practical than he at first seems. He cares for his subjects, rules fairly, and plans his marriage for love around the needs of the kingdom. So it is with surprise and confusion that he tries to understand his betrothed. She isn’t the sweet, intelligent girl he has been writing to. There is a cold side, an aggressive side that doesn’t make sense. Confusion becomes suspicion and eventually he turns to several women he can trust to help him figure it all out.<br /><br />Recognizing the fairy tale that was being wove I started trying to out think it. All the clues were there. Look how smart I am putting them all together! Aha you think you are so clever but I have figured out the mystery at the half way point. I am enjoying this so keep on writing but…oh wow. Didn’t see that coming. Should have, those clues were there too but I sat there distracted by the more obvious ones. Well then Marillier, this round goes to you.<br /><br />Nothing fancy here, just great characters and a wonderful story. The only truly evil villains are minor players (though a few others make a run at the title at times) and the fae influence seems to be an easy way to set up the story rather than anything with lasting influence. Those who can’t take some fairy tale conveniences in plot set up may be disappointed but once the pieces are in play there is very little to pick at.<br /><br />Recommended with full enthusiasm. One of the best books I have read this year.<br /><br />5 Stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="6618774658522556246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1428920196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17152368640475813683"><b>WHAT A WAY TO START OFF MY 2016 READING YEAR</b><br/><br/><b>LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE</b><br/><br/>Firstly, lets just get this out of the way. <u>Everybody back the hell away from Grim</u>. <b>I want to marry him and have his babies</b>. He's the new leading man in my life. Sorry <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/916758907' rel='nofollow noopener'>Terrible</a> . Grim has stolen my heart. <b>LOVE HIM</b>.<br/><br/>This was a wonderful story. <i>Yes</i>, I knew where it was going 100 pages in. <i>Yes</i> Blackthorn lives up to her name, being prickly at times, she's quick to anger, slow to trust and sometimes is downright unlikeable. But she l</span>
  <span id="freeText17152368640475813683" style="display:none"><b>WHAT A WAY TO START OFF MY 2016 READING YEAR</b><br /><br /><b>LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE</b><br /><br />Firstly, lets just get this out of the way. <u>Everybody back the hell away from Grim</u>. <b>I want to marry him and have his babies</b>. He's the new leading man in my life. Sorry <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/916758907" rel="nofollow noopener">Terrible</a> . Grim has stolen my heart. <b>LOVE HIM</b>.<br /><br />This was a wonderful story. <i>Yes</i>, I knew where it was going 100 pages in. <i>Yes</i> Blackthorn lives up to her name, being prickly at times, she's quick to anger, slow to trust and sometimes is downright unlikeable. But she learns from her mistakes, does the best she can and the way she is with Grim is just heartwarming. <i>Yes</i> Prince Oran is quite the idiot and creates problems for himself often. But in the end, <b>it all worked</b>. It all clicked and it all flowed and it all came to life around me and I could barely put it down.<br /><br />The only reason I didn't give this five stars is that the world building and lore of the magic seemed a little sketchy to me, it was all a little bit <i>ambiguous</i> and as result I couldn't give it top marks. Grim deserves five stars all to himself though. <b>LOVE YOU GRIM</b>.<br /><br />This was a wonderful fantasy tale that had a little bit of despair, a touch of magic, a pinch of hope, a sprinkling of mystery and a bunch of love. <br /><br /><b>I thoroughly enjoyed it, I had trouble putting it down, and I've already put the sequel on hold at my library</b>. <br /><br /><b>4</b> <i>marry-me-grim</i> <b>Stars</b><br /><br />Thanks for the buddy read you wonderful people over at <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalo</a>
</b>!</span>

<div id="review_1392974255" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1392974255" />
    <a title="Althea Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann"><img alt="Althea Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1392974255?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1392974255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12523925077323920045">After being unfairly imprisoned by a cruel lord, the healer/wise woman Blackthorn is freed by an enigmatic fey and charged with his rule: for seven years she may not seek revenge for the wrongs done to her and hers; instead she must take up residence in the kingdom of Dalriada and must provide aid to anyone who asks her for help.<br/><br/>Although reluctant, Blackthorn does as she is bid, and sets out for Dalriada, accompanied by her former fellow prisoner, Grim, a giant of a man whose feelings for Blackt</span>
  <span id="freeText12523925077323920045" style="display:none">After being unfairly imprisoned by a cruel lord, the healer/wise woman Blackthorn is freed by an enigmatic fey and charged with his rule: for seven years she may not seek revenge for the wrongs done to her and hers; instead she must take up residence in the kingdom of Dalriada and must provide aid to anyone who asks her for help.<br /><br />Although reluctant, Blackthorn does as she is bid, and sets out for Dalriada, accompanied by her former fellow prisoner, Grim, a giant of a man whose feelings for Blackthorn hover somewhere in the realm between courtly love and devoted worship.<br /><br />Arriving in Dalriada, the pair stumble into a scenario that will be extremely familiar to any reader familiar with the fairytale, 'The Goose Girl.' The local lord, Prince Oran, has been betrothed to a woman he's never seen. However, through extensive and intimate correspondence, he's fallen in love with Lady Flidais in absentia. However, the woman who arrives, although she physically matches the portrait of Flidais, seems to have an utterly different personality from that which he came to expect through the letters he's treasured. Is the change caused by shyness? Trauma due to the death of Flidais' maidservant during the journey? Or were the letters written by an artful scribe, not Flidais herself? All of Oran's associates pretty much tell him to suck it up - but eventually, he'll request Blackthorn's help, which she is honor-bound to give.<br /><br />I liked a lot about this book. The writing is lovely, and the story is a nice mesh of original and traditional fairytale elements. Characters' actions spring naturally from their personalities and past experiences; and I liked that on occasion, it's shown that conclusions based on past experiences can be the result of fallibility. However, there was also a lot I didn't like about the book, especially as it went on. Throughout the entire story (including the subplots), there was a persistent thread of the idea that "good girls don't." (And 'nice' men don't either, or if they do, it's a moral failing.) Certainly, rape and abuse is a horrible thing, and certainly there are women who use sex as a tool of manipulation. But what's portrayed here goes past that, and into the realm of "enjoying sex is a sign of a bad character." I'm not on board with that message.<br />Moreover, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[while the fake-Flidais is certainly not a very likeable person, NOTHING she did warranted the extremely harsh punishment that the readers are clearly supposed to be on board with. Seriously, she's self-centered, inconsiderate of others, and lustful (oh, what a sin!) but in reality, she simply tried to make the best of a difficult and bewildering situation. I found the attitude that we're expected to take toward her comeuppance disturbing. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />My other criticism is that, if we regard this book as a stand-alone, the fey exists solely as a deus ex machina. His motivations are never revealed. I assume that more will come out in the sequel(s), but taking this book on its own, it feels like a structural flaw.<br /><br />I've only read one other book by Marillier so far, and liked it very much - so I'm definitely going to continue on with the sequel to this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12523925077323920045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

And I’m still not sure how to classify it. <br/><br/>Dark, dreamy and magical story that is part fairytale part mystery solving/investigation.   <span id="freeText7881720683761323532" style="display:none">Morrigan’s britches! This is quite a tale. And I’m still not sure how to classify it. <br /><br />Dark, dreamy and magical story that is part fairytale part mystery solving/investigation. Two unlikely partners pushed to work together by ever-meddling fey to unravel mysteries that seemed to have stepped straight from the myths. There is a prince looking for one true love, strange personality changes, a misbehaving dog, an ancient wood and a pool of dark magic, disappeared village girl and mysterious death.<br /> <br />Whenever I thought I figured it out - the story surprised me. At first I thought it will be romantic – it turned out much more grim-dark, when I thought it will be all about magic/paranormal threat – dark human nature appeared to have played a big part. Two main characters aren’t exactly level-headed or wisecracking detectives – as they are fighting rage and demons of their own dark past.<br /><br />Slow burning but engaging and atmospheric read. <br /><br />Recommend for readers of darker fairytales, fey and Celtic mythology fans. <br /></span>

<div id="review_988323211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/988323211" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/988323211?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer988323211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6600152573151820863"><b> *** 4.25 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with my friends at MacHalo group, where fantasy is our life!</b><br/><br/>Dreamer's Pool is a fairy-tale fantasy of the kind that seems familiar, but is new, and haunting, and beautifully written... It draws you in, cocoons you with comfort and mystery, and keeps you there with the debt of characters and promises of a feast at the end of the road. <br/><br/>This is the first Juliet Marillier book I have ever read and am here to declare that it is not going to be the last!!! She writes in a qui</span>
  <span id="freeText6600152573151820863" style="display:none"><b> *** 4.25 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with my friends at MacHalo group, where fantasy is our life!</b><br /><br />Dreamer's Pool is a fairy-tale fantasy of the kind that seems familiar, but is new, and haunting, and beautifully written... It draws you in, cocoons you with comfort and mystery, and keeps you there with the debt of characters and promises of a feast at the end of the road. <br /><br />This is the first Juliet Marillier book I have ever read and am here to declare that it is not going to be the last!!! She writes in a quiet, but beautiful way, without overwhelming the reader with any extra distractions, using a deliberate style to lead you through the riddles of the plot, and delivers a satisfying, if well foreshadowed conclusion. The last is never a problem for me - we all know how certain stories end, but what makes them special is the way we get there. <br /><br />The books' main heroes are Blackthorn, a tortured soul with tragic past, which has rendered her spirit and left her with nothing else to live for but revenge, and Grim, a quiet giant with "a face only mother could love", and a temper, which loss of control has landed him in many of bad situations, leaving him with the belief that he is unworthy of love or human caring. Time has left deep scars in their souls, their bodies are older beyond their ages, their faith in all good and pure lost long ago.... After long term incarceration in a filthy prison where they meet, circumstances conspire to bring them together on an adventure to a foreign land. Blackthorn is bound by a promise she has made to a Fae for the next seven years and Grim feels he has to protect and take care of her, despite of Blackthorns' resistance to the idea and her prickliness. Enter the prince and his betrothed, making a mess of our guys' plans to live quietly and intrigue free. <br /><br />The prince and his girl are paragons of virtue and can get too over the top with their holier-than-thou personas, but it worked OK for the fairy-tale it is. There is somewhat of a menage going on at one point with a servant and a dog, but that will make sense once you guys get to reading it!!! I liked the way other secondary characters had just as much debt as their importance required and no needles "fat" in the setting and world building, despite of the many possible occasions where that might have been a temptation. <br /><br />I am a sucker for fairy-tales and have to admit that this might influence my rating, but to those who enjoy such, I heartily recommend this book and hopefully, the series. This book would be appropriate for all ages, I think, maybe PG 13, not exactly sure - kids nowadays grow up fast. There is no gratuitous violence and as all such stories, we root for the good guys:) <br /><br />Thanks once again to the MacHalos and especially Casey for picking this one for the monthly read! I thoroughly enjoyed it!!! <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6600152573151820863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7882879482002187855">4.5 Stars<br/><br/>First off I want to comment on the absolutely BEAUTIFUL cover! OMG I ADORE THIS COVER! Even though I have no idea who it is meant to depict, as the main character in this series has bright red hair, I DON’T CARE! It’s bloody gorgeous!<br/><br/>This story follows Blackthorn and Grim, they escape an awful prison and with some magical help, they find their way to a kingdom run by crown Prince Oran, who is having some lady troubles. Blackthorn soon becomes the town healer and Oran calls upon her for </span>
  <span id="freeText7882879482002187855" style="display:none">4.5 Stars<br /><br />First off I want to comment on the absolutely BEAUTIFUL cover! OMG I ADORE THIS COVER! Even though I have no idea who it is meant to depict, as the main character in this series has bright red hair, I DON’T CARE! It’s bloody gorgeous!<br /><br />This story follows Blackthorn and Grim, they escape an awful prison and with some magical help, they find their way to a kingdom run by crown Prince Oran, who is having some lady troubles. Blackthorn soon becomes the town healer and Oran calls upon her for some assistance.<br /><br />Yes that was an awful synopsis, but I don’t want to spoil the story for you. It isn’t exactly a romance as much as it is a tale of great friendship and with typical Marillier style, Fae and magic are in abundance.<br /><br />I loved it. I thought it was fantastic. The characters were well developed, there were some absolutely hilarious moments as well as a lot of touching ones. I didn’t quite give it five stars because it was a bit long-winded at times and there was a large lack of romance for my liking. Especially for a Juliet Marillier book.<br /><br />I also guessed the plot twists from the very beginning, but It didn’t hamper my enjoyment of it.<br /><br /><b>Did I enjoy the audio version?</b><br />YES! Loved the three narrators! Oran was by far my favourite. Scott Aiello was fantastic! I have listened to a few books with his narration now and I have enjoyed them all. A good narrator makes all the difference!<br /><br /><b>Would I Recommend Dreamer’s Pool?</b><br />Yes, anyone who enjoys a good Celtic fantasy will love this one. I can’t wait to listen to the second one to see what Blackthorn and Grim get up to next!<br /><br /><i>I purchased Dreamer’s Pool at my own expense at audible.com</i><br /><br />For more reviews check out my:<br /><a href="http://www.melsbookshelf.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a><br /> <a href="http://www.instagram.com/mels_book_shelf" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a><br /> <a href="http://www.twitter.com/melsbookshelf" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a><br /> <a href="http://www.facebook.com/melsbookshelfAU" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a></span>

<div id="review_1592232590" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1592232590" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1592232590?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1592232590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer510660014580775535"><i>“It’s hard, sometimes, not to make things your business.”</i><br/><br/><b>What is the key to writing a successful novel? That is an easy question. A great main protagonist. And the best characters are those built on a conflict where opposites attract and merge.</b> Like, a firefighter non-stop playing with fire (both figuratively, e.g. having an affair, and in reality, e.g. all the time fiddling with his old-school gasoline lighter). Like a mercenary with a charitable heart and a penchant for embroidery. Like a cran</span>
  <span id="freeText510660014580775535" style="display:none"><i>“It’s hard, sometimes, not to make things your business.”</i><br /><br /><b>What is the key to writing a successful novel? That is an easy question. A great main protagonist. And the best characters are those built on a conflict where opposites attract and merge.</b> Like, a firefighter non-stop playing with fire (both figuratively, e.g. having an affair, and in reality, e.g. all the time fiddling with his old-school gasoline lighter). Like a mercenary with a charitable heart and a penchant for embroidery. Like a cranky healer, who hates people. <br /><br />You like the last one? Meet Blackthorn. <b>How refreshing after the crowd of boring angelic herbalists</b>, which are something of Ms Marillier’s expertise. She is a fiery redhead, snappish and contrary <i>“with an intensity about her like that of a wild creature caged,”</i> with a tooth missing and a face that wore its years hard. And yet, under this worn out, beaten-down exterior, the woman she might has been still lingers.<br /><br /><i>“Part of me has turned wild, and another part’s turned dark as an endless night.”</i><br /><br />This mouthy, uncompromising woman is compelled to strike a bargain with mysterious fey: In exchange for her life she needs to serve people for 7 years and must not deny a single cry for help either verbalised explicitly or implicitly aimed at her. For Blackthorn, this is the worst penance you could imagine. <br /><br /><b>Blackthorn carries the novel almost exclusively on her shoulders</b>. She has caught my attention from the very first page. She is unorthodox, neither your sweet angelic creature who'd been wronged and craves for justice nor an anti-heroine on the shady side of life. Her internal contradictions are further emphasised by her companion, a skulking might of muscles called Grim. <br /><br /><i>”He had the look of a fighter, the head shaven, the nose crooked, the eyes small, the neck and shoulders bullish. His was a face only a mother would think handsome.”</i><br /><br />Awesome characterisation, no? He is a man of few words, and all of those carefully selected: <i>“The giant grunted in response. It could have meant yes, no, or Move away before I do you an injury.”</i> His POV is very convincing and sometimes even entertaining if you like this kind of narrative crudeness. <br /><br />Together Blackthorn and Grim complement and balance each other and their relation, as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18965736-dreamer-s-pool-feb-17-2018" rel="nofollow noopener">Silvana pointed out</a> is very similar to this of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1480195669?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Shara and Sigrud</a>. <br /><br />I have to say that I liked this novel much more than the books from the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1600030169?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Sevensweaters series</a>. Firstly, it reads faster. Secondly, I welcomed the change of narrative. In addition to the very distinct main heroine, the multi-POV narration is an added value. <br /><br />Having said this, Dreamer’s Pool is not free from flaws. <b>You need more than an enticing protagonist to charm a reader</b>. My problem with how Marillier’s books are presented resurfaces yet again: <b>the events heralded in the blurb take place well into the second half of the novel</b>. It basically means that <b>we know what is going to happen during the initial 2/3 of the book and the final 1/3 is painfully obvious</b>. Yes, the book is <b>terribly predictable and occasionally boring (travelogue!)</b>. Additionally, Grim is not so very fleshed out as a character <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ why has this silent, stray dog, appointed himself as Blackthorn’s companion and protector? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I do hope there will be more than muscle to his story.<br /><br />Overall, interesting opening to a series with potential for further improvement. You might give it a try. <br /><br />---<br /><br />Also in the series: <br /><br />2. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2332412970" rel="nofollow noopener">Thower of Thorns</a><br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2370161672" rel="nofollow noopener">Den of Wolves</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="510660014580775535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1396603450" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1396603450" />
    <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy"><img alt="Stacey is Sassy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474185067p2/12062194.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1396603450?book_show_action=true">Sep 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey is Sassy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey is Sassy" href="/user/show/12062194-stacey-is-sassy">Stacey is Sassy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781743517024" href="/book/show/24330677-dreamer-s-pool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=para-fantasy-series">para-fantasy-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12062194-stacey-is-sassy?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1396603450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11619946175740293236"><b>From prison to wise woman…with a little help from Grim.</b><br/><br/>I read <i>Dreamer’s Pool</i> in book form…as in paper. I haven’t read a book with paper in years and I admit, I tapped a few times before I remembered to turn the page. I also kept looking to the top of the page to check the time. Who’d have thought that the act of turning pages in a book would become unfamiliar? By halfway I’d stopped tapping luckily and was fully engrossed in this wonderful tale full of adventure, mystery, magic and romance.<br/><br/>When </span>
  <span id="freeText11619946175740293236" style="display:none"><b>From prison to wise woman…with a little help from Grim.</b><br><br>I read <i>Dreamer’s Pool</i> in book form…as in paper. I haven’t read a book with paper in years and I admit, I tapped a few times before I remembered to turn the page. I also kept looking to the top of the page to check the time. Who’d have thought that the act of turning pages in a book would become unfamiliar? By halfway I’d stopped tapping luckily and was fully engrossed in this wonderful tale full of adventure, mystery, magic and romance.<br><br>When I started <i>Dreamer’s Pool</i>, I was intrigued with the gritty and dark start to the story. Intolerable conditions had left Lady (aka Slut and Filthy Whore) beaten and nearly broken. Her fellow inmates were in the same condition, but the prisoner opposite, Grim, was always there to talk to in her darkest hour. The story starts the night before she is set to face the council to tell her story. Her imprisonment was due to her speaking out against the Chieftan of the area, Mathuin. He is an evil man and her life and thoughts are consumed with revenge against the injustices performed at his hands. She is approached by one of the Fey, Conmael, who has a proposition for her. If she is willing to abort her plans for revenge, he will help her escape. There are conditions that need to be filled and at first Lady is hesitant. She must leave, return to her old career as a wise woman and healer and head towards an unknown place with a new name, Blackthorn. She eventually accepts the conditions and finds herself on a new path…with Grim following close behind.<br><br>Grim hasn’t had it easy either. He was a giant of a man who’s nickname was Bonehead. Grim has a wee bit of a temper and a few times we see the red haze descend and take away his control. With no faith in himself, he feels comfort in Blackthorn’s company. He follows her to protect her, liking the feeling of purpose it gives him. To be honest Grim was my favourite character.<br><br>Their journey takes them to Dalriada where they serve as magical healer and handyman under the rule of Prince Oran. Prince Oran is himself on a journey…to true love. He is betrothed to a beautiful maiden named Flidais. They have been corresponding for some time and feel they would make a good match. Unfortunately on her journey to Oran an accident happens and Flidais’ maid is killed. When Flidais and her party arrive Oran is excited to see her. It doesn’t take Oran long to realise that the woman in front of him, might not be his dream woman after all.<br><br>Blackthorn, Grim and Oran must come together to work out mysteries and intrigues within Dalriada. Each face their own challenges and find help and support from the people of Dalriada, Conmael and each other.<br><br>While not my normal read, it was very enjoyable. Julie Marillier has an amazing ability to make you see the world she has created and believe that magic is real. I was in the head of each character and could feel the anguish, despair and loneliness each felt. I also enjoyed working through the mysteries with the characters and felt the satisfaction when everything was solved.<br><br><b>I received a complimentary copy of this book via the publisher, Pan Macmillan Australia, in exchange for an honest review.</b><br><br><a href="http://staceyissassy.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440643271i/16004133._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="48" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/Sassyreviews" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440644070i/16004243.jpg" width="40" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="https://www.pinterest.com/Stacey1565/" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440644070i/16004244.jpg" width="40" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a href="https://www.twitter.com/StaceyisSassy" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1440644070i/16004245.jpg" width="40" height="40" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><a></a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11619946175740293236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_637867447" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/637867447" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4255477-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398251387p2/4255477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/637867447?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/4255477-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21894013-dreamer-s-pool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=2016-read">2016-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4255477-angela?shelf=soon">soon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer637867447" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14484466300933617929">26 April 2020: <a href='https://amzn.to/2xSL6H0' rel='nofollow noopener'>$1.99 on Kindle</a><br/><br/>The first Juliet Marillier book I read was <i>Shadowfell</i>, and I adored it. I adored that whole series. I've been anxious, ever since, to pick up another book/series by her for a long time.<br/><br/>Finally, I was able to squeeze this start to a new fantasy series in. <i>Dreamer's Pool</i> is the first book in the <b>Blackthorn and Grim</b> series. And the two title characters, I absolutely adore.<br/><br/>We first meet them both in a prison. Blackthorn thinks tomorrow is to be her "day in court," so to</span>
  <span id="freeText14484466300933617929" style="display:none">26 April 2020: <a href="https://amzn.to/2xSL6H0" rel="nofollow noopener">$1.99 on Kindle</a><br /><br />The first Juliet Marillier book I read was <i>Shadowfell</i>, and I adored it. I adored that whole series. I've been anxious, ever since, to pick up another book/series by her for a long time.<br /><br />Finally, I was able to squeeze this start to a new fantasy series in. <i>Dreamer's Pool</i> is the first book in the <b>Blackthorn and Grim</b> series. And the two title characters, I absolutely adore.<br /><br />We first meet them both in a prison. Blackthorn thinks tomorrow is to be her "day in court," so to speak. Unfortunately, the powers that be have different plans - ones that will result in Blackthorn never seeing the light of day. Grim has the cell across from her. His only thought is of her safety, even when he knows what is to happen.<br /><br />That night, a mysterious visitor appears offering a deal that's too good to be true. Yet, what choice does Blackthorn have but to accept it. This delays her vengeance and justice for seven long years, but the alternative - no justice at all - is unbearable. So Blackthorn accepts, and makes the long journey north as bid....with Grim following along behind.<br /><br />This is told in multiple first-person points-of-view. There's Blackthorn, Grim, and the prince of Dalraida - Oren. I really enjoyed all of their voices, even though Grim's stuttered way of thinking did take me a bit to get used to. I appreciated how different their voices truly were, how unique they were to themselves. And I can't help but want to know more - especially about Grim's past. <br /><br />The story itself meanders a bit to get to the point. For a good deal of the book I <i>know</i> what happened, even if I can't figure out how. So it was <i>slightly</i> frustrating that it took so long for everyone else to figure out. Granted, we had everyone's point-of-view, and they only had their own, but still, that's one of the disadvantages of this kind of storytelling.<br /><br />All the same, I did enjoy the pace and the world. This is a beginning, a fairy-tale-like set-up to this new world. We get bits and pieces, and just the barest mention of magic. I'm dying to see what Conmael is up to (and who he actually is to Blackthorn). I already mentioned wanting more of Grim's past. And I'm eager to see Blackthron settle more into herself - though I know (and am glad) that her thirst for justice/vengeance will not wait for eternity....maybe just long enough to see it done.<br /><br /><i>Dreamer's Pool</i> didn't grab me quite as completely as <i>Shadowfell</i> did, but I am definitely happy I read it, and excited to go on in the series.<br /><br />3.5 Stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14484466300933617929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1083619393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1083619393" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1083619393?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083619393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15274470272884484707">***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2014/10/review-dreamers-pool-by-juliet-marillier.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>Dreamer's Pool by Juliet Marillier<br/>Book One of the Blackthorn and Grim series<br/>Publisher: ROC Hardcover<br/>Publication Date: November 4, 2014<br/>Rating: 5 stars<br/>Source: Review copy sent by the publisher<br/><br/>Summary (from Goodreads):<br/><br/>In exchange for help escaping her long and wrongful imprisonment, embittered magical healer Blackthorn has vowed to set aside her bid for vengeance against the man who destroyed all that she once held dear. Followed by a former prison mat</span>
  <span id="freeText15274470272884484707" style="display:none">***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2014/10/review-dreamers-pool-by-juliet-marillier.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />Dreamer's Pool by Juliet Marillier<br />Book One of the Blackthorn and Grim series<br />Publisher: ROC Hardcover<br />Publication Date: November 4, 2014<br />Rating: 5 stars<br />Source: Review copy sent by the publisher<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />In exchange for help escaping her long and wrongful imprisonment, embittered magical healer Blackthorn has vowed to set aside her bid for vengeance against the man who destroyed all that she once held dear. Followed by a former prison mate, a silent hulk of a man named Grim, she travels north to Dalriada. There she'll live on the fringe of a mysterious forest, duty bound for seven years to assist anyone who asks for her help. <br /><br />Oran, crown prince of Dalriada, has waited anxiously for the arrival of his future bride, Lady Flidais. He knows her only from a portrait and sweetly poetic correspondence that have convinced him Flidais is his destined true love. But Oran discovers letters can lie. For although his intended exactly resembles her portrait, her brutality upon arrival proves she is nothing like the sensitive woman of the letters. <br /><br />With the strategic marriage imminent, Oran sees no way out of his dilemma. Word has spread that Blackthorn possesses a remarkable gift for solving knotty problems, so the prince asks her for help. To save Oran from his treacherous nuptials, Blackthorn and Grim will need all their resources: courage, ingenuity, leaps of deduction, and more than a little magic.<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />I've never read anything by Marillier, but I've heard such wonderful things about her and her books. I love fantasy, and there are some adult fiction writers whose fantasy I've always wanted to read. Marillier is one of those authors. I have no doubt that I will be reading more of her books (pre- or post-published) in the future!<br /><br />Just so we're clear - this book is NOT Young Adult fiction, it's adult fiction. The protagonists are NOT young adults. Blackthorn is probably in her late twenties, Grim is probably about the same (or older), and the prince is twenty-two and about to be married (so *maybe* he could be considered a young adult. Maybe. But not really). <br /><br />Blackthorn has been granted escape from prison by exchanging her desire for vengeance for her services to the services of the people of Dariada. There, with a former prison-mate, she will serve as a wise woman (basically, a healer). Meanwhile, the prince of Dalriada is getting ready to become betrothed to a lady Flidais, whom he has fallen in love with through their letters. An accident in Dreamer's Wood causes one of her maids to drown in Dreamer's Pool, and the lady is not the same after the drowning. The prince suspects that there is something wrong with the lady, and enlists Blackthorn and Grim's help in the matter. Something is amiss, and it will take some wit and magic to figure it out.<br /><br />At first, I thought this book was all about Blackthorn, an angry woman who has spent a year in prison for trying to go after a nobleman who has been raping and impregnating innocent woman. But this book is also about Grim, a quiet and gruff man who has been quietly serving his sentence for an unknown crime. And it is also about a young prince who believes in romance and dreams and does not have a taste for blood sport and other things that princes should love. This book tells the story of all three of these people, and how their paths intersect.<br /><br />I love this book. I love each character's story. I think the prince was my favorite perspective to follow - which is surprising, because the book starts with Blackthorn's, then Grim's, then Oran's (the prince). Usually, I like the character whose perspective I've seen first the most. But I liked them all! <br /><br />Blackthorn is bitter over her past, and she has every right to be. She hates that she has to spend seven years in the service of those who need her help, before she can seek her vengeance. But she does a world of good for the people of Dalriada, especially the prince. Without her help, the situation with lady Flidais would not have been solved.<br /><br />I'm glad that Blackthorn let Grim stick with her, and that Grim stuck around for as long as he did. Don't get the wrong idea - they are NOT lovers, or in love, or anything like that. They are platonic, friends if anything, but not really friends? They trust each other, they work together well, they make an excellent team.<br /><br />The romance lies in the prince's story, but even that is not really romance... the romance in this book is very subtle and very not-so-important, compared to the other main plots of the book. Oran is totally in love with the lady who wrote him letters, but the lady who appears to him, the lady who went through a traumatic experience when her maid drowned in Dreamer's Pool, is not the same lady. His notions of romance and dreams of love are splintered when he realizes that he will never have that kind of marriage.<br /><br />So there is a mystery to this book - I could not WAIT to find out how things would end. What is wrong with Lady Flidais - is she an impostor, or did she deceive the prince in her letters by having a scribe write them, or is she just completely traumatized over the entire experience of traveling to Winterfalls and then her maid drowning, etc.? I knew the ending would have to be all sorts of epic, and I was not disappointed. <br /><br />The fantasy of this book is flawless. Wait - that makes it sound like the fantasy is part of this book, but that's wrong, because the fantasy IS the book. The world-building is beautiful and carefully constructed and excellent. I love the fantasy world that Marillier has created. It isn't explosive and remarkable and epic, but it is intricate and haunting and fascinating. <br /><br />This book wrapped up really neatly, so I'm interested in seeing how this series continues. Hopefully we get to see how Blackthorn continues to struggle with her seven-year-sentence against vengeance. Maybe she will get a happy ending, at the end of the series. One can hope!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />I can't really think of anything to say in this section, woohoo! Not that any book is perfect, but I can't think of anything.<br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />I so would! I loved this book by Marillier, so I definitely want to read more of her books. I always hear about her amazing fantasy and breathtaking romance - I was hoping for more of that romance in this book, but somehow, with the way this story was woven, I wasn't disappointed. Fantasy in adult fiction - for those of you who love this, check out this book!<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />5 stars. Well deserved, well earned. I'm so glad I decided to give this book (and author) a try. If you're interested, there is a giveaway happening on Goodreads until October 28th!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15274470272884484707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1111519237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1111519237" />
    <a title="Magirosa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32541869-magirosa"><img alt="Magirosa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417481915p2/32541869.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1111519237?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Magirosa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Magirosa" href="/user/show/32541869-magirosa">Magirosa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lori</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32541869-magirosa?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32541869-magirosa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1111519237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11654494310019898731">Overall:<br/><br/>Sigh. Big Sigh. I am disappointed in this book for the strangely harsh treatment of female sexuality. However, I must also say, that I love the Blackthorn and Grim characters and would love to read more of their emergence into this strange new life to which they have committed themselves. I also have such a longstanding respect for Ms. Marillier that I will chalk this one up to an unfortunate derailment.<br/><br/>Elements I like: <br/><br/>Friendship as a central theme: I love how Ms. Marillier introduces t</span>
  <span id="freeText11654494310019898731" style="display:none">Overall:<br /><br />Sigh. Big Sigh. I am disappointed in this book for the strangely harsh treatment of female sexuality. However, I must also say, that I love the Blackthorn and Grim characters and would love to read more of their emergence into this strange new life to which they have committed themselves. I also have such a longstanding respect for Ms. Marillier that I will chalk this one up to an unfortunate derailment.<br /><br />Elements I like: <br /><br />Friendship as a central theme: I love how Ms. Marillier introduces the complex and sometimes challenging friendship between Blackthorn and Grim. I love the slow unfurling of each character’s backstory as well as the developing trust and reciprocal respect and affection that grows. These are two of my favorite characters amongst so many beloved ones in Marillier’s impressive collection.<br /><br />Geis: I really enjoyed the prominent use of a geis as the motivation and challenge for Blackthorn and by extension Grim. I think that this is such a wonderfully nuanced theme to play with. I enjoy Blackthorns struggles and frustration with it, even as it is in some ways calling her to be her best self.<br /><br />Conmeal’s Character: Ah, in addition to Blackthorn and Grim, I have a real interest in learning more about this mysterious fey character, layer of geis and sometimes protector. More please. <br /><br />Mystery: There is something lighter and fresh about this book, which I think may be owing to the mystery form the story follows. I have loved Ms. Marillier's books since I first read Daughter of the Forest and revel in the complexity and depth to which she is unafraid to delve. However, I find, somewhat to my own surprise, that I also can appreciate this book’s more brisk pace. <br /><br />Multiple Points Of View: Something that I rarely like is when the narrative switches between two or more 1st person POV. Often this device is used to get into the antagonist’s POV and something about that unusually irritates me. However, in this case I find that I look forward especially to the contrasting and building narrative between Blackthorn and Grim. I appreciate how the voice for all three characters is nuanced and genuinely feels like the thoughts of three individuals.<br /><br />Elements that I didn’t like:<br /><br />SPOILER ALERT!<br /><br />Sexual Girl is Evil: It truly pains me to write this. I have loved all of Ms. Marillier’s books and have grown to trust her handling of women in her writing. There are often difficulties that arise for the female characters in the male dominated power structures in which they exist in her books and I have always found that the author handles these complex circumstances with appropriate demonstrations of strength, tenacity and intricacy. As a result, the author in past books has somehow managed the difficult task of communicating the mores of the culture and time without seeming to fall into sex shaming.<br /><br />However, as I progressed through Dreamers Pool I was disturbed to find that there was a pervasive theme of sex shaming. More specifically, with the introduction of the growing suspicion surrounding Flidais’s character, I began to notice that the warning bells were being set off repeatedly by her sexual overtures to Oran. What I mean is that, while she does say several things that seem inappropriate to the queenly Flidais of Oran’s imaginings, it was really her sexual manipulations and dramatically inappropriate sexual overtures (witnessed by others beyond even Oran himself) that make it clear to the characters and, more importantly, to the reader that she could not possibly be the real Flidais.<br /><br />Here is what troubles me about this:<br /><br />I find it regrettable that the only consensual sex featured in this book full of rape and pervasive abuse of female characters (which in Blackthorn’s and the village girl’s cases lead nearly to their deaths), is used as a primary basis for establishing the antagonist’s character as nefarious, manipulative and dangerous. <br /><br />Oran refers to Flidais’s sexuality as her “weapon” more than once. Weapon, really? This seems so extreme and falls painfully into a lexicon of sex shaming from which we, as a culture, are trying so painfully to extricate ourselves. This is the same basic principle that supports the notion that women must behave and dress in certain ways in order to mask their inherently dangerous sexuality, else men will be powerless and victimized. This worldview is why female rape victims are asked what they were wearing with a startling frequency whereas male rape victims are seldom interrogated in this way. I mention this because what we read does affect how we think and I have long loved the type of female characters and how they are portrayed in Ms. Marillier’s work. I was disappointed to see her reflecting a set of beliefs that are truly damaging to our young women: one where virginity and sexual modesty are paramount for determining a woman’s value.<br />When it is revealed that the Flidais character isn’t really the noble born Fidelis but instead just a low born commoner Ciar it implies only women of less regal bearing, those more base and common, would express sexual agency. <br /><br />Ciar’s singular “crime” is being sexually manipulative. In my opinion, looking objectively, Ciar’s character is essentially an innocent. She is caught up in magic that is out of her control; that she didn’t desire nor orchestrate and cannot reverse, let alone even understand. Yes, her response to keep it secret after she witnesses her own physical body’s death, may be regrettable but hardly evil. And perhaps keeping it a secret is even understandable; who should she tell? Would she even be believed or would she more likely risk being simply shut away as presumably insane? From this vantage point she seems to have a horrible fate assigned to her, for being essentially a victim. This seems like a life/death sentence (life span of a dog is so much shorter) for her character whose only wrongdoing, besides being petty and less progressive in her thoughts (yet still comparable to her contemporaries), is that she is not a virgin and likes sex.<br /><br />End comments on this topic: I would have preferred that there were other actions taken by Flidais/Ciar to merit her as the as the book’s primary antagonist. The way the book is currently structured, I would have rather done without the sexual aspect of Flidais/Ciar’s character all together. I think that it would have more clearly communicated her character’s weakness and lose nothing with the omission. I also could have done without everyone who knew Ciar when she was a servant having to mention her sexual behaviors. It just seemed surprisingly one-dimensional for our key antagonist and far below the normal complexity with which Ms. Marillier typically handles her villains.<br /><br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11654494310019898731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3721054-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325525682p2/3721054.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/554662079?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/3721054-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21894013-dreamer-s-pool">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721054-jo?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3721054-jo?shelf=fantasy-sci-fi">fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer554662079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13639609885895548982">November 3-5, 2015<br/>So I was just going to read the first part of this book to remember the characters and such, but the story just drew me in and I found myself reading it again and enjoying it very much!<br/><br/>November 4-8, 2014<br/>I am so glad I splurged and bought this book the day it was released. It was truly a great book, and it ranks right up there with my two other favorite Marilliers - Heart's Blood and Daughter of the Forest. Blackthorn and Grim are some of the most flawed yet perfect characters I</span>
  <span id="freeText13639609885895548982" style="display:none">November 3-5, 2015<br />So I was just going to read the first part of this book to remember the characters and such, but the story just drew me in and I found myself reading it again and enjoying it very much!<br /><br />November 4-8, 2014<br />I am so glad I splurged and bought this book the day it was released. It was truly a great book, and it ranks right up there with my two other favorite Marilliers - Heart's Blood and Daughter of the Forest. Blackthorn and Grim are some of the most flawed yet perfect characters I have ever read. Their tale broke my heart. It always hurts to know just how evil humans can be to one another. We never get to hear Grim's backstory though which was pretty clever on Marillier's part. If you needed a reason (which I don't) to read the next book, learning Grim's tale would be a good one. <br /><br />The story was magical. So much so that I wanted to savor each word and draw out the book, yet I rushed toward the ending to see the outcome. You really come to care about the characters and want to see things work out. Even the secondary characters are fleshed out and realistic. <br /><br />I loved the shout out to Daughter of the Forest letting us know that Sorcha and her brothers were not too far removed from this story. I have so many books in the TBR pile, but all I really want to do is lose myself in a Marillier book even if it is one I have already read. There is something about her writing draws you in and keeps you spellbound. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13639609885895548982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1631364630" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1631364630?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/8575414-emma">Emma</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1631364630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7703933427095106575">4.5 stars. My first Juliet Marillier and I picked a good one! I liked our world weary and flawed main characters Blackthorn and Grim. Loved the dreamy fairy tale quality to the story, it seemed timeless and magical. I will definitely read the next in this series. <br/>I am still not sure if the rest of Juliet Marillier's books will be for me, despite how much I loved this one. I often see the word 'romantic' used to describe her work and I'm quite picky about what romance I can tolerate! So if anyone</span>
  <span id="freeText7703933427095106575" style="display:none">4.5 stars. My first Juliet Marillier and I picked a good one! I liked our world weary and flawed main characters Blackthorn and Grim. Loved the dreamy fairy tale quality to the story, it seemed timeless and magical. I will definitely read the next in this series. <br />I am still not sure if the rest of Juliet Marillier's books will be for me, despite how much I loved this one. I often see the word 'romantic' used to describe her work and I'm quite picky about what romance I can tolerate! So if anyone can recommend anything else by this author, all suggestions gratefully received.</span>

<div id="review_3112338533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3112338533" />
    <a title="Charlotte" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte"><img alt="Charlotte" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487528389p2/11475773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3112338533?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte" href="/user/show/11475773-charlotte">Charlotte</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3112338533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1937061760991302583"><i>“Part of me has turned wild, and another part’s turned dark as endless night, and I’m not going to change back just because someone says I must.”</i><br/><br/>Today's book is <i>Dreamer's Pool</i> by Juliet Marillier, a 2014 fantasy novel. Spoilers follow, as well as a discussion of sexual violence.<br/><br/><b>So What's It About?</b><br/><br/><i>In exchange for help escaping her long and wrongful imprisonment, embittered magical healer Blackthorn has vowed to set aside her bid for vengeance against the man who destroyed all that she once held d</i></span>
  <span id="freeText1937061760991302583" style="display:none"><i>“Part of me has turned wild, and another part’s turned dark as endless night, and I’m not going to change back just because someone says I must.”</i><br /><br />Today's book is <i>Dreamer's Pool</i> by Juliet Marillier, a 2014 fantasy novel. Spoilers follow, as well as a discussion of sexual violence.<br /><br /><b>So What's It About?</b><br /><br /><i>In exchange for help escaping her long and wrongful imprisonment, embittered magical healer Blackthorn has vowed to set aside her bid for vengeance against the man who destroyed all that she once held dear. Followed by a former prison mate, a silent hulk of a man named Grim, she travels north to Dalriada. There she'll live on the fringe of a mysterious forest, duty bound for seven years to assist anyone who asks for her help.<br /><br />Oran, crown prince of Dalriada, has waited anxiously for the arrival of his future bride, Lady Flidais. He knows her only from a portrait and sweetly poetic correspondence that have convinced him Flidais is his destined true love. But Oran discovers letters can lie. For although his intended exactly resembles her portrait, her brutality upon arrival proves she is nothing like the sensitive woman of the letters.<br /><br />With the strategic marriage imminent, Oran sees no way out of his dilemma. Word has spread that Blackthorn possesses a remarkable gift for solving knotty problems, so the prince asks her for help. To save Oran from his treacherous nuptials, Blackthorn and Grim will need all their resources: courage, ingenuity, leaps of deduction, and more than a little magic.</i><br /><br /><b>What I Thought - The F Word</b><br /><br />The first and most important thing to say about this book is that I absolutely love Blackthorn and Grim as a duo. Grim, especially, is a revelation of a character in his patience, gentleness, loyalty, and the quiet assumption that Blackthorn doesn't really need him. He's easily one of the best characters I've encountered in this reading challenge, and together the two of them create that same magical feeling that Heart's Blood did for me- there's an oddball couple of characters who have been hurt by the world and band together to find strength in kindness towards each other, learn and grow and face the world together. It's a beautiful, beautiful moment when Blackthorn finally realizes and tells Grim that she does in fact need him. These moments of bonding and quiet camaraderie truly make the book the special thing that it is.<br /><br /><i>Dreamer's Pool</i> is also deeply concerned with the matter of violence against women, whether it is related to Blackthorn's own experiences in prison, the misdeeds of the man who put her there or the first "case" that B &amp; G solve, where a man named Branoc abducts and rapes a girl named Ness. There are some interesting moment relating to respectability politics and slut-shaming in Branoc's trial, including the way that the community was willing to dismiss Ness's absence by writing her off as a "bad girl" come to bad ends. There is also a clear tie in this story between privilege and its abuse, shown in Mathuin's misdeeds and the way that his status protects him and enables him to continually destroy those who would stop him. Finally, I really appreciated Marillier's attention to Blackthorn's trauma schemas and cognitive distortions, including the protecting misandry that so often arises as a result of abuse by men. <br /><br />My main struggle with this book has to do with Marillier's inclusion of a major plot line where a (lying, conniving, manipulative) woman falsely accuses a man of rape. I'll be the first to admit that my reaction to this plot point is a visceral knee-jerk at best because of how disbelief in rape accusations relates to my own painful experiences. I don't know if there is any way for me to get around that gut-level emotional reaction, and it's possible that another reader without a similar background might react to this plot point entirely differently.<br /><br />I do think there's a case to be made, however, for the fact that my anger represents a bigger trend - one of the worst (and most common) things a survivor of sexual violence may face is the denial and disbelief in their story from friends, family, and the legal system.  After going through one of the worst things a person can possibly go through, it can be just as traumatizing to hear someone dismiss your pain and say "I don't believe you, you're just trying to get him in trouble."<br /><br />It's not that false rape accusations don't happen, or that I think authors shouldn't talk about them - but given what survivors of sexual violence face in the form of blame and disbelief I think it's essential to de-mythologize the myth of the pervasive false rape accusation as often as possible. With that in mind, I don't necessarily agree with Marillier's decision to give it the same amount of emphasis in her narrative as the stories of true violence against women. When we look at the <a href="https://www.google.com/search?q=false+rape+accusations+graph&amp;client=firefox-b-d&amp;sxsrf=ALeKk02gn2JqhHBGS5fMk8F0l7yZZqok6g:1585808959697&amp;source=lnms&amp;tbm=isch&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=2ahUKEwjWseXdjsnoAhWKsJ4KHXpJCIEQ_AUoAnoECAsQBA&amp;biw=1072&amp;bih=512#imgrc=kfDBgOL3IlqR3M" rel="nofollow noopener">scale</a> of the problems, it becomes immediately apparent to me that a narrative with equal emphasis on false rape accusations and actual rape is perpetuating a distorted view of the issue that simply hurts survivors more than they have already been hurt. <a href="https://medium.com/rachael-writes/the-myth-of-the-false-rape-accusation-f40d456dc78e" rel="nofollow noopener">Here</a> is a great article if you're interested in reading more about it. <br /><br />I don't think I've struggled more to convey my thoughts in the time that I've been writing these reviews, so I hope that what I've said makes some sense. In sum, the inclusion of false rape accusations in <i>Dreamer's Pool</i> left me shaken for Personal Reasons, yes, but I also believe that those Personal Reasons speak to a truth that is at the heart of the way our society facilitates sexual violence - the overwhelming doubt and minimization we cast on the experiences of survivors and our willingness to make excuses for the accused. In pursuit (intentional or not) of this goal, many people uphold the myth of the incredibly common false rape report even though it has no bearing in reality.  It's possible that I'm grasping at straws here because I just can't see beyond my own intense feelings about this issue informed by trauma - but on the off chance that I'm actually onto something, I think it does bear mentioning.<br /><br />I also feel like trapping Ciar in the dog's body was much too harsh a punishment for what she did, given the desperation of her circumstances and her belief that no one would believe her. If I were Blackthorn I would have Branoc (the rapist) and Ciar The Dog change bodies. Ciar could continue her life, abeit in a different body, and then Branoc would live the rest of his life as a little dog, unable to rape anyone else. This solution would also tidy away one of my other concerns about Dreamer's Pool's take on sexual violence - Branoc's "rehabilitation" guarantees absolutely nothing as it is. There is absolutely nothing about his punishment that will address the underlying reasons that he abducted Ness, and he could easily manipulate his way into convincing Oran that he is redeemed and harmless now. <br /><br />I absolutely 100% want to read more stories with Blackthorn and Grim together, however. Here's hoping that my next encounter with these two provides a little less in regards to rage-inducement. <br /><br /><b>About the Author</b><br /><br />Born in New Zealand in 1948, Juliet Marillier was educated at the University of Otago  with a BA in languages and a Bachelors in Music. She worked as a high school and university level music teacher, an opera singer and choral conductor before becoming an author full time. She is an active writing mentor, gives many writing workshops and remains active in her local writing community. She is a member of  The Order of Bards, Ovates and Druids and lives with a "pack" of rescue dogs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1937061760991302583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
